Objection and First Answer: World's Possibility in Pre-Eternity
Objection about the world's possibility in pre-eternity and the mutakallimun's first answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mutakallimun's first argument that God is a voluntary agent, based on the impossibility of an eternal world and the necessary causal connection.

Core Idea
God's pre-eternal existence does not force an eternal world; He is a voluntary agent.

This lesson presents a philosophical objection against the mutakallimun's proof that God is not a necessary agent, followed by their first response. The objection tries to force a dilemma: either the world was possible in pre-eternity or not. The mutakallimun answer by showing that the combination of two impossibilities—that an effect can lack its cause and that the world is pre-eternal—proves that the cause must be voluntary.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector presents two alternatives about the world's possibility in pre-eternity. Read carefully to see the dilemma.
Notice the phrase 'فإن قيل' introducing the objection.
2
Understand the dilemma
If the world was possible in pre-eternity, then it must be eternal. If it was impossible, then perhaps the pre-eternal cause did not necessitate it. Identify each horn.
The second alternative leads to the mutakallimun's response.
3
Examine the first answer
The mutakallimun combine two impossibilities: the effect's non-existence after the cause (impossible) and the world's pre-eternity (impossible). From this they deduce the cause was not necessary.
They argue that if the cause were necessary and existed in pre-eternity, the effect would have to exist in pre-eternity, but that is impossible.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Since the cause is pre-eternal but the effect is temporal, the cause must be a voluntary agent (فاعل بالاختيار) rather than a necessary agent.
This preserves God's pre-eternity while affirming the world's temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: العالم إما أن يكون ممكن الوجود في الأزل، وإما أن لا يكون ممكن الوجود في الأزل. فإن كان ممكن الوجود في الأزل فحينئذ يلزم قدم العالم، وليس لكم أن تقولوا: إنه محال أن يكون العالم قديماً، لأن هذا التقدير هو تقدير أن كون العالم أزلياً، ليس بممتنع. وإن كان محال الوجود في الأزل. فنقول: على هذا التقدير، لم لا يجوز أن يقال: العلة القديمة لوجود العالم، وإن كانت موجودة في الأزل، لا يلزم منها كون العالم أزلياً، لأنه كما أن حال المؤثر معتبر في حصول الأثر، فكذلك حال القابل معتبر، وأولى الأحوال بالاعتبار كونه ممكناً في نفسه، فإذا كان الإمكان ثابتاً في الأزل، لم يلزم من حصول العلة الموجبة في الأزل حصول الأثر في الأزل؟ أجاب المتكلمون عنه من وجهين: الأول: أن نقول: تخلف المعلول عن العلة محال، وكون العالم قديماً أيضاً محال. وهذان المعنيان لما اجتمعا علمنا أن العلة الموجبة للعالم ما كانت موجوداً في الأزل. وقد كان المؤثر الأزلي موجوداً في الأزل، فعلمنا أن ذلك المؤثر ما كان موجباً بالذات. بل كان فاعلاً بالاختيار.
If it is said: The world is either possible of existence in pre-eternity, or not possible of existence in pre-eternity. If it is possible of existence in pre-eternity, then the pre-eternity of the world follows, and you cannot say that it is impossible for the world to be pre-eternal, because this supposition is a supposition that the world being pre-eternal is not impossible. And if it is impossible of existence in pre-eternity, then we say: On this supposition, why is it not permissible to say: The pre-eternal cause of the existence of the world, even if it existed in pre-eternity, does not necessitate the world being pre-eternal, because just as the state of the effecter is considered in the attainment of the effect, so also the state of the recipient is considered, and the state most worthy of consideration is its being possible in itself. So if possibility is established in pre-eternity, does it not follow from the existence of the necessitating cause in pre-eternity the existence of the effect in pre-eternity? The mutakallimun answered it in two ways: The first: That we say: The effect's non-existence subsequent to the cause is impossible, and the world being pre-eternal is also impossible. When these two meanings are combined, we know that the necessitating cause of the world was not existing in pre-eternity. And the pre-eternal effecter existed in pre-eternity, so we know that that effecter was not necessary by essence, but was a voluntary agent.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This is an objection (فإن قيل) against the proof that God is not a necessary agent. The objector proposes two alternatives: either the world is possible in pre-eternity (الأزل) or not. If it is possible, then why couldn't the necessary cause produce it in pre-eternity, leading to an eternal world? The mutakallimun answer that the effect's non-existence after the cause is impossible, so if the cause were necessary and present in pre-eternity, the effect would necessarily exist in pre-eternity. But the world is temporal, so the cause cannot have been necessary. Instead, the cause must be voluntary (فاعل بالاختيار), meaning it could choose to create at a later time. The first answer states that since both the impossibility of the effect's non-existence after the cause and the impossibility of the world's pre-eternity are true, we deduce that the cause was not existing in pre-eternity as a necessary cause, but as a voluntary agent. This preserves God's pre-eternity while affirming the world's temporality.

Key Terms
الأزل
ممكن الوجود
محال الوجود
علة موجبة
فاعل بالاختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun deny that God's causality is eternal.
Correction: They affirm God's pre-eternal existence but deny that His causality necessitates an eternal effect. He is a voluntary agent who creates in time.

Checkpoint
The mutakallimun's first answer to the objection relies on the combination of which two impossibilities?
A) Impossible for effect to follow cause and impossible for God to exist.
B) Impossible for effect to follow cause and impossible for world to be pre-eternal.
C) Impossible for cause to precede effect and impossible for world to be temporal.
D) Impossible for God to be eternal and impossible for world to be temporal.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun's first answer shows that because an eternal world is impossible, the pre-eternal cause cannot be a necessary cause, hence it must be a voluntary agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God was not compelled to create you, but chose to do so out of His free will, how does that change the way you view your own existence and your obligations to Him? What would you say to Him tonight in prayer about this?
?
The objector tried to corner the mutakallimun with a logical dilemma, but God's action transcends human logic. Are there areas in your life where you try to box God into your expectations or demands, forgetting that He is the free, voluntary Lord? Will you repent of that today?
?
The mutakallimun's answer rests on combining two impossibilities. What impossible demands do you make of God in your heart—demands that He should act according to your timing or your understanding? How can you surrender those to His perfect will?
